    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText6950930321365087767" style="display:none">There was a large audience assembled on the 14th of January, 1862, at the session of the Royal Geographical Society, No. 3 Waterloo Place, London. The president, Sir Francis M -, made an important communication to his colleagues, in an address that was frequently interrupted by applause. This rare specimen of eloquence terminated with the following sonorous phrases bubbling over with patriotism: "England has always marched at the head of nations" (for, the reader will observe, the nations always march at the head of each other), "by the intrepidity of her explorers in the line of geographical discovery." (General assent). "Dr. Samuel Ferguson, one of her most glorious sons, will not reflect discredit on his origin." ("No, indeed!" from all parts of the hall.)</span>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/35307992-mike-mcdougal">Mike McDougal</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It was indeed an effort to finish this book. But please don't let that discourage you from exploring other science fiction by Jules Verne. "From the E<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It was indeed an effort to finish this book. But please don't let that discourage you from exploring other science fiction by Jules Verne. "From the Earth to the Moon" was much more interesting!<br />Also, the science in "From the Earth to the Moon" is surprisingly accurate. Glance at NASA's synopsis: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://er.jsc.nasa.gov/seh/vernorig.html">https://er.jsc.nasa.gov/seh/vernorig....</a><br />For example, Verne predicted 3 Americans would go to the moon, with the launch site being in Florida, and mission control in Houston.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5566632517721581910">Cinq semaines en ballon = Five Weeks in a Balloon (Extraordinary Voyages, #1), Jules Verne <br/>Five Weeks in a Balloon, or, Journeys and Discoveries in Africa by Three Englishmen (French: Cinq semaines en ballon) is an adventure novel by Jules Verne, published in 1863. It is the first novel in which he perfected the "ingredients" of his later work, skillfully mixing a plot full of adventure and twists that hold the reader's interest with passages of technical, geographic, and historic description. T</span>
  <span id="freeText5566632517721581910" style="display:none">Cinq semaines en ballon = Five Weeks in a Balloon (Extraordinary Voyages, #1), Jules Verne <br />Five Weeks in a Balloon, or, Journeys and Discoveries in Africa by Three Englishmen (French: Cinq semaines en ballon) is an adventure novel by Jules Verne, published in 1863. It is the first novel in which he perfected the "ingredients" of his later work, skillfully mixing a plot full of adventure and twists that hold the reader's interest with passages of technical, geographic, and historic description. The book gives readers a glimpse of the exploration of Africa, which was still not completely known to Europeans of the time, with explorers traveling all over the continent in search of its secrets.<br />عنوانها: 5 هفته پرواز با بالون؛ پنج (5) هفته در بالون؛ پنج هفته پرواز با بالون بر فراز افریقا (مترجم: ایرج حیدری؛ انتشارات سپیده، 1362، در 141 ص)؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: سال 1962 میلادی<br />عنوان: پنج هفته در بالن؛ اثر: ژول ورن؛ مترجم: عنابت الله شکیباپور؛ تهران، غزالی، 1354؛ در 248 ص؛ چاپ دیگر: تهران، گنجینه، 1363؛ در 248 ص؛ <br />عنوان: پنج هفته پرواز با بالون، مترجم: نفیسه دربهشتی؛ قدیر گلکاریان؛ منوچهر حمیدی؛ حسین چهرنور؛ پروانه بنی یعقوب؛ سلماز بهگام؛ <br />پروفسور فرگوسن می‌خواهند برای سفری اکتشافی به آفریقا بروند، اما برای دوری از قبایل نامتمدن و حیوانات وحشی برای سفر بالن را برمی‌گزینند و از دوست خود «کندی» نیز دعوت به همکاری می‌کند، خدمتکار خود «جو» را نیز که فردی باهوش و زرنگ است، با خود همسفر کند، برای پرواز دادن بالن، آن را با کشتی به جزیره‌ ای در نزدیکی آفریقا در شهر غزه پیاده می‌شوند، و مردمان آن‌ها را با خدای خود یعنی ماه اشتباه می‌گیرند، و آن‌ها سلطان را که بیمار بوده نجات می‌دهند، و به راه خود ادامه می‌دهند، در یک شب فریاد کمک فردی را می‌شنوند، و به کمک که معدن طلاست خاک می‌کنند، و مقداری طلا برمی‌دارند، اما با کمبود آب و همچین نبود باد برای به حرکت درآوردن بالن مشکلاتی پیش میآید، سرانجام پس از تحمل بی آبی، توفانی درمی‌گیرد و آن‌ها را به سمت جنگل و       <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ian" href="/user/show/2741551-ian">Ian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/11082887-cinque-settimane-in-pallone">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2741551-ian?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2741551-ian?shelf=adventures">adventures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2741551-ian?shelf=racism">racism</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer263879811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3611542183880697367">Verne's first full-length novel, while setting the formula for many of his later books, is definitely not one of his best: the science is sketchy and the plot is basically a series of small misadventures in a row that the three main characters escape with usually not too much difficulty and a just modicum of ingenuity. <br/><br/>The book would still be enjoyable enough, however, if not for the blatant racism that permeates all the pages where they meet another human being: every single black person in Afr</span>
  <span id="freeText3611542183880697367" style="display:none">Verne's first full-length novel, while setting the formula for many of his later books, is definitely not one of his best: the science is sketchy and the plot is basically a series of small misadventures in a row that the three main characters escape with usually not too much difficulty and a just modicum of ingenuity. <br /><br />The book would still be enjoyable enough, however, if not for the blatant racism that permeates all the pages where they meet another human being: every single black person in Africa is either a savage killer (or a cannibal, or a bandit, or engaged in perverted rituals), or gullible and prone to worship our heroes as lunar deities; in any case, incapable of real civilization. The Arabs fare only a little better, in that they are rich and have fine cities, but then are all ruthless and intent on killing the infidels. This is way more than I'm able to tolerate even for a novel written in the 1850s, and the rest of the novel doesn't really make up for it.</span>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2425528527" />
    <a title="Mary ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37766180-mary"><img alt="Mary ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555156334p2/37766180.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2425528527?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary ♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary ♥" href="/user/show/37766180-mary">Mary ♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2425528527" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15293860182237496819">3.5/5 stars<br/><br/><b> As for difficulties," replied Ferguson, in a serious tone, "they were made to be overcome. </b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534579997ra/26149117.gif' width='200' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><u> Pros of reading a Victorian Era classic </u><br/><br/>♦ Complicated vocabulary, detailed descriptions and lots of facts about the time period. Now, if you didn't know, I happen to be an avid fan of everything Victorian, because it is an era that really intrigues me, something that means reading this was a big plus for me. <br/><br/>♦ Really progressive science facts. All of the books Jules Verne has written are cleve</span>
  <span id="freeText15293860182237496819" style="display:none">3.5/5 stars<br><br><b> As for difficulties," replied Ferguson, in a serious tone, "they were made to be overcome. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1534579997ra/26149117.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u> Pros of reading a Victorian Era classic </u><br><br>♦ Complicated vocabulary, detailed descriptions and lots of facts about the time period. Now, if you didn't know, I happen to be an avid fan of everything Victorian, because it is an era that really intrigues me, something that means reading this was a big plus for me. <br><br>♦ Really progressive science facts. All of the books Jules Verne has written are cleverly created, made in such a way that was considered science fiction back there. It is no wonder that most of the journeys he talked about have actually been fulfilled, and in this case, it was also not surprising to see how well he handled scientific knowledge and technological progress, especially since in the Victorian era people had found themselves in a very quick, life changing technological advance.<br><br>♦ Mannerism, strong platonic bonds that I really enjoyed and lack of overwhelming plot points, that would have tired me or made me lose my interest. The friendship between the three men in this book was very powerful and well spun, and I found myself smiling at a lot of scenes because of the way they cared about each other.<br><br>♦ Exploration of religion, faith, loss, hope, dreams and morals, in a way that was very innovative, refreshing and thought-provoking. The main characters were not power hungry and they rarely dwelled in obsessions with goods, as they had to survive some really severe conditions<br><br><u> Cons on reading a Victorian Era classic </u><br><br>♦ Blatant racism<br><br>♦ Sometimes too overwhelming descriptions. At some point, there was basically almost an entire chapter that was names and dates of other explorers. I know that this proves the author did a large, methodical research, and it was good to learn some new things, but it still made me want to skip to the next chapter quickly at some point.<br><br>Overall, as I happen to really admire Jules Verne, I tried not to dwell on the negative points, because I know that things were different back then and that a lot of classics actually include problematic opinions. I enjoyed reading the book, despite its flaws, and I would recommend Verne for someone who wanted to start reading classics, because he is easier to read than most and has very clever plots and character building.<br><br>Until my next review (which will not be in points, I'll be back in full on reviews xD), I will see you soon, wonderful people ♥<br><br>Stay strong and keep reading ♥<br>~Mary<br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15293860182237496819" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1435251928" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1435251928" />
    <a title="Benjamin Stahl" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl"><img alt="Benjamin Stahl" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592923113p2/16968146.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1435251928?book_show_action=true">Nov 06, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Benjamin Stahl" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Benjamin Stahl" href="/user/show/16968146-benjamin-stahl">Benjamin Stahl</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9782253005902" href="/book/show/1452982.Cinq_semaines_en_ballon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16968146-benjamin-stahl?shelf=classics">classics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1435251928" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9709199692124025610">I enjoyed this story <i>so much more</i> than I thought I would. Having read <i>20,000 Leagues Under The Sea</i> a while back, I was already familiar with the writing of Jules Verne. And while that book was very good, there were also some flaws ... such as the writer's tendency to bog the narrative down with long-winded, heavily technical descriptions regarding the scientific processes and theories related to his story. <br/>These parts I felt slowed the pace too much. But they were always compensated for, with so</span>
  <span id="freeText9709199692124025610" style="display:none">I enjoyed this story <i>so much more</i> than I thought I would. Having read <i>20,000 Leagues Under The Sea</i> a while back, I was already familiar with the writing of Jules Verne. And while that book was very good, there were also some flaws ... such as the writer's tendency to bog the narrative down with long-winded, heavily technical descriptions regarding the scientific processes and theories related to his story. <br>These parts I felt slowed the pace too much. But they were always compensated for, with some very exciting and intense moments of action and suspense to regain my attention. Overall, <i>20,000 Leagues</i> was a perfectly good novel, but a little unbalanced in the way it was told. Given the premise - (that of an elaborate, accommodating submarine, which traverses the oceanic globe in search of its underwater mysteries) - I couldn't help but feel that it could have been <i>even better</i>. <br><br>I approached <i>this</i> story with more of an obligatory sense that I ought to give Jules Verne another go. I just happened to purchase this awesome hardback book last winter, which is titled <i>Four Novels</i>, and compiles, respectively, <i>Five Weeks In A Balloon</i>, <i>Journey To The Centre Of The Earth</i>, <i>20,000 Leagues</i>, and <i>Around The World In Eighty Days</i>. <br>Admittedly, I bought this mostly because it makes any bookshelf look awesome.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448449254i/17142358._SY540_.jpg" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The reason I took so long reading it was because I probably spent half the time gazing at the front cover, tracing my finger over the indentations admiringly. The pages were also gold-tipped, and I restricted myself to only reading this inside the house - (no chucking it into my work bag or reading it in the bath) - and every time I handled it, I washed my hands and then thoroughly dried them. This book was like a bed-ridden child to me, only not so demanding. <br><br>I won't bore or irritate anyone with a rehash of the plot. I'll just give the very basic premise, which is that an esteemed British doctor - (or engineer, or whatever) - has invented a balloon that runs on hydrogen and stuff, and with this contraption, he and two accomplices intend on flying over central Africa - (back in those days, a very wild and unexplored part of the world, the centre of which was left only to the imagination of Western civilisation) - from the eastern coastal island of Zanzibar ... <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448449254i/17142359._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Which, by the way, I decided was going to be my next holiday destination ( ... until I realised the price for even getting there) ...</b><br><br>And then to the western coast, the exact point of which is "left to providence". I'll have to admit that initially, I wasn't at all interested in this story. Balloon have never really done much for me. And even the concept of flying over Africa wasn't that appealing ... you know, cause I'm an asshole. It didn't excite my imagination quite as much as a submarine journey does. And the idea also reminded me of two stories written by Poe - <i>The Balloon Hoax</i> and <i>The Unparalleled Adventures Of One Hans Pfaall</i>, which were okay stories, but nothing to get too excited over. <br><br>Things start off rather smoothly, but as it's a Jules Verne story, and as it needs to be at least somewhat exciting, this trio find themselves pitched against obstacle after obstacle. Every single danger they run into gets more and more thrilling, and even though one generally expects the heroes to pull through, Verne managed to make me question several times how things were going to end up. There are some surprises throughout the novel, and sometimes it got more intense and violent and scary than I thought it was ever going to. It's honestly the best kind of adventure story one could ask for. It appeals to that inner-child mentality like an early Steven Spielberg film, and in fact, I'm surprised that this hasn't been remade more recently by Hollywood. The only film adaptation I know of was back in 1960's or something. This is one of those books where I would say, "Hey, you know if I ever became a successful director - I know it'll never happen, but hypothetically, you know - well if I was ever a director, this is one of those books I would personally try and turn into a blockbuster film". <br><br>The climax especially, as the balloon continues to wither and sink, was fantastically tense and had me glued to its pages. It's awesome that a book from way back in 1863 can still hold someone in 2015 riveted to its story. It had me that way, at any rate. I expected at least the beginning to be a little slow, but seriously it gets good straight away. Before long at all, I had to acknowledge that I was <i>really</i> enjoying it. About halfway, I realized that I loved the story and was pretty much decided that, unless something fucked up happened and the tale got boring, that I was gonna give it four stars. But when I neared the end, I just couldn't deny the feeling that I really ought to give it a perfect rating. And since the book just got progressively better and better - (I enjoyed it much more than <i>20,000 Leagues</i>) - and since the ending was perhaps the most exciting part, there's just no way I can give it anything lower. At least not for a while. Sometimes I'll look back on a book retrospectively, and decide it wasn't as good as I initially thought it was (like with <i>American Psycho</i> and <i>Jaws</i>). But this more often works the other way, as with <i>Huckleberry Finn</i> and ... shit, what else was there? Oh, <i>War Of The Words</i>. <br><br>But yeah, for now I'm perfectly content to give this five stars. It was a very good novel, in my opinion, and though I understand that it's not considered up there with Verne's greatest work by most of his fans, it's easily my favourite of the two books I've read of his so far. And now I'm going to very carefully replace this beautiful book back into the shelf and leave it untouched for a while, before continuing with <i>Centre Of The Earth</i>, which, incidentally, I am now much more interested in reading, having enjoyed this book so much. <br> <br><br><br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="9709199692124025610" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1093649286450417874">Ok, ok, so the book is racist but it's also just bad. So bad that after weeks of putting it aside and trying to muster up the strength to slog through to the end, I gave up, read about it online, and have no regrets. <br/><br/>Having never explored Jules Verne, I was inspired to read his work after adoring "All the Light We Cannot See", in which the sea-loving female protagonist reads "20,000 Leagues Under the Sea" and "Around the World in 80 Days". I bought a gorgeous collection of 4 of his novels and st</span>
  <span id="freeText1093649286450417874" style="display:none">Ok, ok, so the book is racist but it's also just bad. So bad that after weeks of putting it aside and trying to muster up the strength to slog through to the end, I gave up, read about it online, and have no regrets. <br /><br />Having never explored Jules Verne, I was inspired to read his work after adoring "All the Light We Cannot See", in which the sea-loving female protagonist reads "20,000 Leagues Under the Sea" and "Around the World in 80 Days". I bought a gorgeous collection of 4 of his novels and started with the first book he wrote which was apparently the one that sold the most copies at the time of its release. Good for them. Maybe they were disappointed and never bought his next books. I will not be dissuaded but I am going to wait a little while before attempting another Verne. <br /><br />So boring! Wow. A lot of senseless dialogue - around 80% of the books is dialogue - between the 3 main characters who talk in such superfluous prose; "My dear Dick!" is used hundreds of times and always during the most pinnacle moments of crisis! They always have time to keep up their polite Victorian manners, even when a group of dangerous, murderous black natives are attacking their balloon but then turn out to be baboons instead ("At a distance there's no great difference"). Oops! What used to be charming, funny, and even exciting in the 1860s is considered cliche, childish, and boring today: Surprise! The best friend who is only pretending to accompany the Doctor on the journey so that he can stop such a life-threatening endeavor actually ends up going along with them! <br /><br />So, here's hoping the next Jules Verne is better and that I am more prepared to handle it.</span>

<div id="review_1377420420" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1377420420" />
    <a title="Czarny Pies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29160274-czarny-pies"><img alt="Czarny Pies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1400687408p2/29160274.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1377420420?book_show_action=true">Aug 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Czarny Pies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Czarny Pies" href="/user/show/29160274-czarny-pies">Czarny Pies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9782253005902" href="/book/show/1452982.Cinq_semaines_en_ballon">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Parents wishing to educate their children about racism.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Czarny by: </span>
      Barbara Eden and Red Buttons
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29160274-czarny-pies?shelf=french-lit">french-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1377420420" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2895214782408276461">Five Weeks in A Balloon is the first novel written by Jules Verne and unquestionably one of his best. Unfortunately it is indeed as its reputation holds highly racist which creates problems about how it should be approached. <br/><br/>Sir Samuel Ferguson the hero of Five Weeks in a Balloon is a member of the Royal Geographic Society who in the the 1850s decides to explore Africa by crossing it from East to West in a balloon accompanied by two endearing sidekicks. Where it works, the descriptions of the ca</span>
  <span id="freeText2895214782408276461" style="display:none">Five Weeks in A Balloon is the first novel written by Jules Verne and unquestionably one of his best. Unfortunately it is indeed as its reputation holds highly racist which creates problems about how it should be approached. <br /><br />Sir Samuel Ferguson the hero of Five Weeks in a Balloon is a member of the Royal Geographic Society who in the the 1850s decides to explore Africa by crossing it from East to West in a balloon accompanied by two endearing sidekicks. Where it works, the descriptions of the camaraderie of the three balloon passengers is as charming as that of Athos, Porthos and Aramis. Unfortunately, the rules of the genre dictate that the three Musketeers / explorers must constantly duel with various enemies. The adversaries are inevitably members of various African tribes which are all extremely brutal and highly uncivilized. The racist tone of the author is certainly unacceptable today. However, as the book was published in 1863 when the U.S. Civil War was still underway, progressives on the both sides of the Atlantic would have been incensed at the revolting picture painted of Blacks through-out the book at the time it appeared.<br /><br />I think it would be a prudent thing for parents to steer their children towards other Verne books such as Journey to the Centre of the Earth, Around the World in 80 Days or the Mysterious Island. However, Five Weeks in a Balloon still has considerable merit. Parents could perhaps explain to their sons and daughters that the racist attitudes of Jules Verne simply shows that very gifted people can be racist, homophobic or Anti-Semitic. These prejudices can be found just as easily amongst the talented and the likeable as amongst the nasty and the talentless. The safe choice however is still to encourage young people to read other things by Verne. In a similar way I think that the Merchant of Venice is the last thing that one should read by Shakespeare.<br /><br />The great thing about Five Weeks in a Balloon is the way in which Verne makes science and history interesting for young people. He describes the technology of hot air balloons in great detail but he does so in a way that the reader is fascinated. Similarly whenever the balloon floats over the path taken by one of the nineteenth century explorers, Verne describes the history of the expedition and the challenges the members encountered. In this way, he provides a wonderful description of the process of exploration and a great narrative of how Europe became acquainted with Africa. Verne truly had a great gift and it is pity how few authors make similar efforts to educate readers of literature about scientific developments.<br /><br />Many young people who have developed a taste for the writing of Jules Verne will enjoy this novel which has many strong points. It is however racist by the standards of our era and by the standards of its time. Many people will be happier not reading it.<br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2895214782408276461" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_10076859" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10076859" />
    <a title="Silvana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/666003-silvana"><img alt="Silvana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600533521p2/666003.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10076859?book_show_action=true">Dec 07, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Silvana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Silvana" href="/user/show/666003-silvana">Silvana</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer2289203612735166790">A late review, because actually I've started reading this book after I've finished reading "Around the World in 80 Days" (two in one). Similar plot, one guy tries to prove that he's capable of doing something that others can only imagine (and cannot). That is why the more I read Verne's books, the more I feel that he's trying to stress human spirit and optimism. If you have the capability, funding and strength to achieve your dreams, go for it and who cares about what others may think. That's th</span>
  <span id="freeText2289203612735166790" style="display:none">A late review, because actually I've started reading this book after I've finished reading "Around the World in 80 Days" (two in one). Similar plot, one guy tries to prove that he's capable of doing something that others can only imagine (and cannot). That is why the more I read Verne's books, the more I feel that he's trying to stress human spirit and optimism. If you have the capability, funding and strength to achieve your dreams, go for it and who cares about what others may think. That's the key message.<br /><br />The theme is an ambitious African exploration using air balloon, from the East Side (Zanzibar) to the West Side (Senegal). At that time (the 19th century), Africa is still regarding a mysterious region with its dangerous beasts, cannibals, tribal wars and extreme environmental condition. This book tells them all, including several description of the journey's made by famous explorers such as Livingstone, Burton and Speke. Quite an eventful journey of three English men: an academician, his servant and a hunter (Yes, there's always an "intellectual" figure in all Verne's books, no doubt about that!) However, the scientific explanation only limited to "how the balloon works".<br /><br />My fave scene would be when the balloon was attacked by condors, the sacrifice made by one of the aeronauts, and the rescue mission for him. It reminds me of Indiana Jones' films.<br /><br />Anyway, if you like these kind of adventure books, I recommend to read H. Rider Haggard's King Solomon's Mines.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2289203612735166790" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3179984391" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3179984391" />
    <a title="Wally Flangers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75111402-wally-flangers"><img alt="Wally Flangers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513621589p2/75111402.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3179984391?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wally Flangers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wally Flangers" href="/user/show/75111402-wally-flangers">Wally Flangers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/24405015-five-weeks-in-a-balloon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3179984391" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6796916581927025034">Excelsior!<br/><br/>Tell me Jules Verne isn’t the man…. Who else can blend an abundance of science, physics, geography, and history into a story line and still make it undeniably enjoyable? Answer: NOBODY…. The dude was WAY ahead of his time. His stories do take a bit of effort and imagination on your part at times, but nobody can open the doors of your mind like Jules Verne can – followed by a couple hits of Cannabis to get the creative juices flowing.<br/><br/>“Five Weeks in a Balloon” (also known as “Journeys an</span>
  <span id="freeText6796916581927025034" style="display:none">Excelsior!<br /><br />Tell me Jules Verne isn’t the man…. Who else can blend an abundance of science, physics, geography, and history into a story line and still make it undeniably enjoyable? Answer: NOBODY…. The dude was WAY ahead of his time. His stories do take a bit of effort and imagination on your part at times, but nobody can open the doors of your mind like Jules Verne can – followed by a couple hits of Cannabis to get the creative juices flowing.<br /><br />“Five Weeks in a Balloon” (also known as “Journeys and Discoveries in Africa by Three Englishmen”) is an adventure novel that was published in 1863. It is book #1 in “The Extraordinary Voyages” series and takes the reader through the immense continent of Africa, which at that time was very mysterious to Europeans. The book was a big hit and put Verne on the map, instantly securing a contract with Jules Hetzel’s publishing house. If this is your first experience with Jules Verne, you will be left thirsting for more….<br /><br />The story is about an explorer named Dr. Samuel Ferguson who, with the help of his loyal manservant Joe along with his friend Dick Kennedy, decide to travel across Africa in a hydrogen-filled balloon. Fergusson comes up with a brilliant way to control the balloon’s altitude to make this journey possible. The purpose of the expedition is said to link the voyages of Sir Richard Burton and John Speke in East Africa with Heinrich Barth in the Sahara region. The balloon starts off in Zanzibar, located on the east coast, and is expected to end on the west coast.<br /><br />The Nile plays an important role and focus on the groups objective, linking the voyages from the other explorers. Through their excursion, the trio face many obstacles and dangers. After all, they are in Africa for God’s sake. Not exactly known to be a safe haven for humans, even today, let alone in the 1800’s…. Not only are there land animals lurking about waiting for you to land your balloon so they can rip your limbs apart and feed them to their young…. But you also have condors flying around with nothing better to do than form an attack squad, as well as armed tribesman and weather elements to deal with. Oh, and did I mention that hydrogen levels and dehydration also play very important roles, factors of which were somewhat overlooked in the game of “Let’s Fly Across Africa Cause We’re Nuts”? Yeah…. The group has a lot of challenges they must overcome to not only successfully complete their objective, but also to survive. Luck (and coincidence) plays a major role throughout their journey providing the reader with an underlying feeling of destiny.<br /><br />“Five Weeks in a Balloon” was extraordinary (no pun intended)…. From beginning to end it was loaded with drama, suspense, adventure, action, etc…. Everything the human mind requires to feel fulfilled. As usual, Jules Verne’s characters were awesome and distinguished. Verne always seems to have a rich, brilliant explorer / scientist heading these expeditions, trailed by an unusually loyal, kiss-ass servant by his side wiling to die for the cause…. And Verne paints their personalities and tendencies extraordinarily (there’s that word again!) well.<br /><br />My only complaint, and what kept this book from reaching the 5 star mark for me, is that it ended rather abruptly. The ending had classic build up but the climax was quite brief. I think it should have dragged out more…. In hindsight, I wanted a little more out of the entire book. You seldom ever hear me say, “this book was too short”…. But, this book could have had more obstacles or extended sections. I think another hundred pages or so would have been perfect….<br /><br />FINAL VERDICT: I give this book 4 out of 5 stars. Although “Five Weeks in a Balloon” is not my favorite Jules Verne novel, it was still terrific and very hard to put down. I didn’t expect to like it as much as I did…. This book is a must read for adventure novel enthusiasts.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6796916581927025034" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/266925583" />
    <a title="Greg F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6248510-greg-f"><img alt="Greg F" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/266925583?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg F" href="/user/show/6248510-greg-f">Greg F</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer266925583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8592458507145104006">While idly wandering through a book store for something to read recently, one book in particular caught my attention - A collection of Jules Verne books, featuring his first novel, Five Weeks in a Balloon. Verne being one of my favorite authors, I had no hesitation in purchasing the hefty book, and soon began to plow through it. The book involves three men (which seems to be a constant in Verne’s fictional universes) and their adventures travelling over the continent of Africa in a hot air ballo</span>
  <span id="freeText8592458507145104006" style="display:none">While idly wandering through a book store for something to read recently, one book in particular caught my attention - A collection of Jules Verne books, featuring his first novel, Five Weeks in a Balloon. Verne being one of my favorite authors, I had no hesitation in purchasing the hefty book, and soon began to plow through it. The book involves three men (which seems to be a constant in Verne’s fictional universes) and their adventures travelling over the continent of Africa in a hot air balloon. After reading for some time, it became apparent that this was the author’s first novel. The narration seems unsteady, or unsure of its wording at times. The book also tends to contain abnormally slow sections where the reader loses interest. It was not the best novel I’ve read, however it was, by far, not the worst. The book set up an excellent premise for Verne and allowed him to set up many writing formulas which were apparent in future novels such as Journey to the Center of the Earth, Around the World in Eighty Days, and Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8592458507145104006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText6095293206089192228" style="display:none">I had a vision that I read all Jules Verne Adventure Books. I read some of his book as a child, this one I missed. I have to say, I was really disappointed and all the reasons you will read under the 1-star and 2-star reviews apply to mine as well.<br />There is racism and actually "white supremacy" there - something that I think was very IN at that time. The africans are all savages and cannibals. The three idiots in the ballon have no doubt about that, they question their origins not a second, they were always white and rich. Beah !<br />There is the idiot with his gun who shoots everything that moves, or at least want to. The way he kills an elephant is really gruesome. <br />There is the servant who is the most idiot of all, he makes some sort of martyrdom to save his master. Were the people so stupid back in those days?<br />Jules Verne has better books than this one.<br />I gave two stars because of some scientific and geographic stuff that i found quite interesting.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11505074999167784347">Cinq Semaines en Ballon is really a road trip story, except the road is the sky and the car is a balloon filled with highly flammable hydrogen. This book is typically entertaining Verne, with it's intelligent and self assured protagonist and series of exotic adventures. It's hard to believe that a balloon could ever have been the high tech, futuristic gadget in a semi-science fictiony adventure story, but balloons were cutting edge in the 1860s and the French would use them inspire the world dur</span>
  <span id="freeText11505074999167784347" style="display:none">Cinq Semaines en Ballon is really a road trip story, except the road is the sky and the car is a balloon filled with highly flammable hydrogen. This book is typically entertaining Verne, with it's intelligent and self assured protagonist and series of exotic adventures. It's hard to believe that a balloon could ever have been the high tech, futuristic gadget in a semi-science fictiony adventure story, but balloons were cutting edge in the 1860s and the French would use them inspire the world during the siege of Paris just a few years after this novel was published. Fun to read and the French couldn't be simpler to understand for students of the language.<br /><br />Unfortunately there are parts of this book that are extremely racist by today's standards, but you have to cut Verne some slack, he wrote this thing 150 years ago.</span>

<div id="review_987466820" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/987466820" />
    <a title="Realini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7873218-realini"><img alt="Realini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420269105p2/7873218.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/987466820?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Realini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Realini" href="/user/show/7873218-realini">Realini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer987466820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7296648066187847804">Five Weeks in A Balloon by Jules Verne<br/><br/>Awe, inspiration, joy, amusement, hope, interest, pride, gratitude, serenity and most of all love... These are the elements, feelings or incentives to feel these emotions that we should look for in the stories we read, in order to obtain Positivity. For the ten mentioned components help one become positive.<br/>Jules Verne has imagined all kinds of trips, machines and technology. From submarines, to machines that fly, float, and submerge do anything. We are taken</span>
  <span id="freeText7296648066187847804" style="display:none">Five Weeks in A Balloon by Jules Verne<br /><br />Awe, inspiration, joy, amusement, hope, interest, pride, gratitude, serenity and most of all love... These are the elements, feelings or incentives to feel these emotions that we should look for in the stories we read, in order to obtain Positivity. For the ten mentioned components help one become positive.<br />Jules Verne has imagined all kinds of trips, machines and technology. From submarines, to machines that fly, float, and submerge do anything. We are taken to the Center of the Earth, around it in an extraordinary eighty days. We take two years holidays, search for the Children of Captain Grant, and submerge for 20,000 leagues and more.<br />He was the absolute dreamer and is an inspiration to SF writers and readers.<br />We are in awe when we think that his imagination was not only fabulous, but accurate. Many of Verne’s predictions proved to be correct.<br />There is also joy and amusement felt when one reads his novels, because quite often they involve exploration of new territory, discoveries of unknown facts.<br />In Five Weeks In A Balloon the participants in the journey discover the springs of the Nile. The story seems rather silly at times. I wonder why it had to start from Zanzibar, even if an explanation regarding the winds is given, it does not appear to hold water.<br />True, in reading such stories, the teenager, for that is the age group which should be interested more in Verne than in hunger Games or Divergent, could be grateful for the adventure, without questioning so much the technology, the real premises and the power of the winds.<br />The balloon is still an interesting means of transportation, and several people have looked and are still looking into making the balloon a more attractive way to fly. In an age when we put so much carbon, sulphur and other toxic gas in the atmosphere, using winds to move around would make sense.<br />There are hazards, plain enough in Five Weeks In a Balloon, where the natives shoot down with arrows the expedition. <br />There is a narrow escape, which could be questioned by a fault finding mind, because once you have holes in the balloon, it seems impossible to lift it up again. But let’s be merit finders and not just fault finders.<br />At another point, the balloon is attacked by…vultures and it is rapidly falling to the ground. In order to save the samples, one of the crew jumps down to sacrifice for the good of science and humanity.<br />There is also a parrot, named Ramses and as an owner of two macaws I fell for the bird, although I can’t help but frown on the fact that it was kept (how?) in a pocket at a certain stage in the tale.<br />All is well if it ends well, but I am not going to reveal the end of a story which involves flying over the lake Victoria on the way to Senegal. The members of the expedition are supposed to arrive in five weeks on the Pacific Coast.<br />Like in other Verne stories- Around The World in eighty days – there is a bet which revolves around the exact time of arrival. <br />If you read it, you will find who won. But I recommend it if you are a teenager, for adults I wouldn’t say this is so exciting. <br />But I may be wrong<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7296648066187847804" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2667771175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2667771175" />
    <a title="Ira Therebel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5902527-ira-therebel"><img alt="Ira Therebel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546421513p2/5902527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2667771175?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ira Therebel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ira Therebel" href="/user/show/5902527-ira-therebel">Ira Therebel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5902527-ira-therebel?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5902527-ira-therebel?shelf=classic-literature">classic-literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5902527-ira-therebel?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5902527-ira-therebel?shelf=africa">africa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5902527-ira-therebel?shelf=adventures">adventures</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2667771175" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12326748828547980708">The first book written by Jules Verne and the first in Extraordinary Voyages series that I began reading. It isn't bad but also not a great read that one would expect from an adventures book by famous Jules Verne. I hope the next ones that I will read will be more exciting.<br/><br/>Three man decide to fly across Africa in a balloon. This is a science fiction for that time and I don't know much about balloons to see how close to reality it was. The descriptions made it seem very realistic which is definit</span>
  <span id="freeText12326748828547980708" style="display:none">The first book written by Jules Verne and the first in Extraordinary Voyages series that I began reading. It isn't bad but also not a great read that one would expect from an adventures book by famous Jules Verne. I hope the next ones that I will read will be more exciting.<br /><br />Three man decide to fly across Africa in a balloon. This is a science fiction for that time and I don't know much about balloons to see how close to reality it was. The descriptions made it seem very realistic which is definitely a good part of the book.<br /><br />The three characters don't have much personality as each of them seems to have only one characteristic. The dialogues are also boring, repetitive and sometimes irritating. Joe's constant jokes were more annoying than funny.<br /><br />When it comes to adventure books the characters are usually secondary to adventures. But the ones in this book are not very exciting. Here and there something happens but it seems to be very short compared to the uneventful times in their balloon. <br /><br />One good part was reading about their discovery of Africa and what they were seeing. Back when it was written ordinary people didn't know much about the continent so I can see how it was exciting for them to read. And for the readers of our time the descriptions are beautiful.<br /><br />Considering that it was written in 19th century it is not surprising that it was pretty racist and full of excitement to kill animals that are now close to extinction. So it is a bit hard to read without cringing but I can see that it is normal for that time and try not to judge. One interesting part though was when Doctor said that Africa will one day be a dominating continent as through time it has always changed.<br /><br />I would have said that while it might not be the best adventure book for adults (still can be a good read) children would find it more interesting. But I guess I would be careful to give my child a book that keeps on describing Africans as dumb savages. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12326748828547980708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2054059287" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2054059287" />
    <a title="Dion Perry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/24059977-dion-perry"><img alt="Dion Perry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475724620p2/24059977.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2054059287?book_show_action=true">Jul 08, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Dion Perry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Dion Perry" href="/user/show/24059977-dion-perry">Dion Perry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2054059287" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17455301927821247480">This is a story of three men’s journey across Africa in a balloon. The story is very dated and written in accordance with the social norms of the day. In this regard, it can be perceived as racist and, given there are no female characters, sexist. However, the story is a classic. It is full of suspense and drama which leaves the reader on the edge of the seat wondering what will happen next. Interestingly, the story has no villain characters, the landscape and the people and animals in it are th</span>
  <span id="freeText17455301927821247480" style="display:none">This is a story of three men’s journey across Africa in a balloon. The story is very dated and written in accordance with the social norms of the day. In this regard, it can be perceived as racist and, given there are no female characters, sexist. However, the story is a classic. It is full of suspense and drama which leaves the reader on the edge of the seat wondering what will happen next. Interestingly, the story has no villain characters, the landscape and the people and animals in it are the villains. I found the actions and attitudes of the characters from this former period to be fascinating particularly noting how they differ from today. It left me wondering how stories from my time will be perceived in a hundred-years time. I look forward to reading more from this author.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17455301927821247480" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer5899656427816026007">I know of Jules Verne’s stories, the major ones anyway, but I’ve never read any of his books. So I thought I’d start with one I knew very little about. And Wow! It was so good! This is a classic example of why he is one of the world’s greatest authors. At no time did I feel like I wasn’t right there with the three adventurers, exploring the wild lands of Africa. The characters felt so real and alive. A great Victorian adventure that I didn’t want to end!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2534125590" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2534125590" />
    <a title="Roger Burk" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2420354-roger-burk"><img alt="Roger Burk" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1247791755p2/2420354.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2534125590?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Roger Burk" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Roger Burk" href="/user/show/2420354-roger-burk">Roger Burk</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2534125590" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4308388171985774990">In 1862 three British adventurers fly a hydrogen balloon across Africa from Zanzibar to Senegal, generally mooring to a tree at night and sleeping on the ground. (One wonders why a French author chose British heroes.) Obliging winds carry them over every interesting site in between, Lake Victoria and the source of the Nile and Lake Chad and Timbuktu--even a bloody tribal battle in progress and the martyrdom of a saintly missionary. They find not Wakanda but another less benign fantasy, one a pro</span>
  <span id="freeText4308388171985774990" style="display:none">In 1862 three British adventurers fly a hydrogen balloon across Africa from Zanzibar to Senegal, generally mooring to a tree at night and sleeping on the ground. (One wonders why a French author chose British heroes.) Obliging winds carry them over every interesting site in between, Lake Victoria and the source of the Nile and Lake Chad and Timbuktu--even a bloody tribal battle in progress and the martyrdom of a saintly missionary. They find not Wakanda but another less benign fantasy, one a product of the writer's time: the natives are childlike, bloodthirsty, depraved, or all three. A frenzied cannibal cuts off an enemy's arm in the middle of a battle and stops to take a bite of the raw flesh. (He is punished with an English bullet in the forehead, of course.)<br /><br />This qualifies as genuine science fiction on two grounds. One is that the journey is made possible by a plausible invention that will allow the balloon to rise and descend without expending either ballast or lifting gas. Another is that the story is carefully linked to actual journeys of exploration in Africa, and accounts of those journeys are frequently discussed by the aeronauts. The story depends on there being a favorable wind generally being available at some height, which is perhaps wishful thinking. Who cares? It's still an engaging and exciting story, if you can stomach the depraved-natives stories.<br /><br />Alas, this translation (Walter) is clunky. I think we are supposed to be entertained by the banter of the three adventurers, but no charm in their conversation comes through.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4308388171985774990" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_956663241" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956663241" />
    <a title="Colleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30274173-colleen"><img alt="Colleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589824510p2/30274173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/956663241?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Colleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Colleen" href="/user/show/30274173-colleen">Colleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30274173-colleen?shelf=debut">debut</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30274173-colleen?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30274173-colleen?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30274173-colleen?shelf=books-for-my-map">books-for-my-map</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30274173-colleen?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30274173-colleen?shelf=survival">survival</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30274173-colleen?shelf=19th-century-and-before">19th-century-and-before</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer956663241" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11036745098899634136"><b>3 Stars</b><br/><br/><i>Five Weeks in a Balloon</i> is the first in Verne's "Extraordinary Voyages" series. And if I'm not mistaken, the first of his books to be published. It very much sets the example of how the rest of that series would go. Although it is evident that he was still finding his style, and I did not enjoy this book as much as some of his later works. But I like to read author's debuts and see how their style and techniques change over time.<br/><br/>This is a classic adventure story wherein three men attempt </span>
  <span id="freeText11036745098899634136" style="display:none"><b>3 Stars</b><br /><br /><i>Five Weeks in a Balloon</i> is the first in Verne's "Extraordinary Voyages" series. And if I'm not mistaken, the first of his books to be published. It very much sets the example of how the rest of that series would go. Although it is evident that he was still finding his style, and I did not enjoy this book as much as some of his later works. But I like to read author's debuts and see how their style and techniques change over time.<br /><br />This is a classic adventure story wherein three men attempt to explore Africa (which was at the time still largely unknown) via a hot air balloon. Verne took some liberties with the science and obviously had to make up some details about things that were unknown, but overall he writes a convincing story. And it is certainly stuffed full of daring escapades and hapless misadventures. It is an interesting combination of science, exploration, and at times very poetic scenic descriptions. <br /><br />But it should definitely be noted that this book is not up to twenty-first century criteria of political correctness and should definitely be taken with a grain of salt.<br /><br /><br />RATING FACTORS:<br />Ease of Reading: 3 Stars<br />Writing Style: 3 Stars<br />Characters: 3 Stars<br />Plot Structure and Development: 3 Stars<br />Level of Captivation: 3 Stars<br />Originality: 4 Stars<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11036745098899634136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2907126825" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2907126825" />
    <a title="Joe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8206910-joe"><img alt="Joe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1441668217p2/8206910.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2907126825?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joe" href="/user/show/8206910-joe">Joe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2907126825" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1307672249669933558">This is a good ... not a great ... action story. It was a very clever futuristic story when written. It has good twists and turns with clever technical solutions to problems. I now recognize the difficulties in controlled balloon travel ... weight vs lift. <br/><br/>It contained a bit too much history of African exploration ... perhaps interesting when the book was written but not today. <br/><br/>This was my first Verne novel. I enjoyed it and look forward to additional books to read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3244312093" />
    <a title="Emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38155631-emma"><img alt="Emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569182777p2/38155631.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3244312093?book_show_action=true">Mar 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma" href="/user/show/38155631-emma">Emma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781406554212" href="/book/show/1934627.Five_Weeks_in_a_Balloon">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3244312093" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2682289174246660861">Struggled to finish it. <br/>The plot was clear and direct but so repetitive and mind-numbing. The characters would face an issue and overcome it without much struggle, never failing to mention how blacks were savages, brutes, barbarians, etc. <br/>I probably shouldn’t bother pointing this out, though, since it seems to be fairly common in 19th century novels about Africa.<br/>All in all, I can’t say I enjoyed but it’s not the worst classic I’ve read.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

		<td>
		    <b>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3iC3/U+A3aUfFeH7J7Om4uCGIlah+/u3nTEfJJqGhNLccYkq8WZCuqBgan7vClSx3ACBV6Oq5KMsm8T5t2MTIQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YVXq+xU6ma6nzYCnitI4mnoSR+wEu2yGRuM+CnPsnWtjBNQsq9wGsRi4CyJCa8rJRpTk7Qbqc5L3SeXXXgkKmA==')})
  }

It was published under the considerably longer original title: The Farther Adventures of Robinson Crusoe; Being the Second and Last Part of His Life, And of the Strange Surprising Accounts of his Travels Round three Parts of the Globe. Although intended to be the last Crusoe tale, the novel is followed by a non-fiction book involving Crusoe by Defoe entitled Serious Reflections During the Life and Surprising Adventures of Robinson Crusoe: With his Vision of the Angelick World (1720).\n\nThe story is speculated to be partially based on Moscow embassy secretary Adam Brand\'s journal detailing the embassy\'s journey from Moscow to Peking from 1693 to 1695.\n\nThe book starts with the statement about Crusoe\'s marriage in England. Este<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText13367433518789883262\" style=\"display:none\">Odată cu primul său volum de nuvele, publicat la Madrid în 1963 și reluat după câţiva ani în România sub titlul celei mai fascinante dintre ele, Mircea Eliade pare să fi găsit tema de elecţie a “realismului magic“, inaugurat de el în literatură. Este o temă pe care o va explora neobosit de acum înainte; ea descinde parcă dintr-o idee recurentă a studiilor şi eseurilor sale de istorie a religiilor. Potrivit ei, omul modern este, chiar fără să o ştie, apăsat de o nemiloasă “tiranie a istoriei”, de care caută cu înfrigurare să se elibereze. Numai că soluţia izbăvirii de această tiranie trece printr-o abolire a timpului, care alcătuieşte miezul acelui vârtej capabil să-l soarbă şi să-l desfiinţeze.\n\nEroul lui Eliade din La ţigănci, un om obişnuit prins în întâmplări oarecare, trăiește experienţa unei fisuri în fluxul timpului, prin care se află proiectat într-o altă lume, familiară şi stranie totodată, o lume ce îi dezvăluie <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4618563167636613974">Jules Gabriel Verne was a French author who pioneered the genre of science-fiction. He is best known for his novels <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54479.Journey_to_the_Center_of_the_Earth' title='Journey to the Center of the Earth' rel='nofollow noopener'>Journey to the Center of the Earth</a>
</i> (1864), <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33507.Twenty_Thousand_Leagues_Under_the_Sea' title='Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea</a>
</i> (1870), and <i>
  <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54479.Around_the_World_in_Eighty_Days' title='Around the World in Eighty Days' rel='nofollow noopener'>Around the World in Eighty Days</a>
</i> (1873). <br/><br/>Verne wrote about space, air, and underwater travel before navigable aircraft and practical submarines were invented, and before any means </span>
  <span id="freeText4618563167636613974" style="display:none">Jules Gabriel Verne was a French author who pioneered the genre of science-fiction. He is best known for his novels <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54479.Journey_to_the_Center_of_the_Earth" title="Journey to the Center of the Earth" rel="nofollow noopener">Journey to the Center of the Earth</a>
</i> (1864), <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/33507.Twenty_Thousand_Leagues_Under_the_Sea" title="Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea" rel="nofollow noopener">Twenty Thousand Leagues Under the Sea</a>
</i> (1870), and <i>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/54479.Around_the_World_in_Eighty_Days" title="Around the World in Eighty Days" rel="nofollow noopener">Around the World in Eighty Days</a>
</i> (1873). <br /><br />Verne wrote about space, air, and underwater travel before navigable aircraft and practical submarines were invented, and before any means of space travel had been devised. He is the second most translated author of all time, behind Agatha Christie. His prominent novels have been made into films. Verne, along with H. G. Wells, is often referred to as the "Father of Science Fiction".</span>

In the novel, First Mate Shandon receives a mysterious letter asking him to construct a reinforced steamship in Liverpool. As he heads out for Melville Bay and the Arctic labyrinth, a crewman finally reveals himself as Captain John Hatteras, and his obsession--to get to the North Pole. After experiencing appalling cold and hunger, the captain treks across the frozen wastes in search of fuel. Abandoned by most of his crew, and accompanied by a rival American explorer, Hatteras continues his journey to the Pole, encountering endless perils and adventures along the way.  This new and unabridged translation of the first of Verne\'s Extraordinary Journeys series brilliantly conveys the novel\'s hypnotic mood and atmosphere. This edition also includes the original, censored ending, and fascinating details about the Arctic expeditions that captivated Verne\'s imagination. Our rocket ship gets shot out of a cannon? To the moon? Goodness! But in other ways it\'s full of eerie bits of business that turned out to be very near reality: he had the cost, when you adjust for inflation, almost exactly right. There are other similarities, too. Verne\'s cannon was named the Columbiad; the Apollo 11 command module was named Columbia. Apollo 11 had a three-person crew, just as Verne\'s did; and both blasted off from the American state of Florida. Even the return to earth happened in more-or-less the same place.
